//! Internal interface for communicating between a `proc_macro` client\\n2: //! (a proc macro crate) and a `proc_macro` server (a compiler front-end).\\n3: //!\\n4: //! Serialization (with C ABI buffers) and unique integer handles are employed\\n5: //! to allow safely interfacing between two copies of `proc_macro` built\\n6: //! (from the same source) by different compilers with potentially mismatching\\n7: //! Rust ABIs (e.g., stage0/bin/rustc vs stage1/bin/rustc during bootstrap).\\n8: \\n9: #![deny(unsafe_code)]\\n10: \\n11: use std::hash::Hash;\\n12: use std::ops::{Bound, Range};\\n13: use std::sync::Once;\\n14: use std::{fmt, marker, mem, panic, thread};\\n15: \\n16: use crate::{Delimiter, Level, Spacing};\\n17: \\n18: /// Higher-order macro describing the server RPC API, allowing automatic\\n19: /// generation of type-safe Rust APIs, both client-side and server-side.\\n20: ///\\n21: /// `with_api!(MySelf, my_self, my_macro)` expands to:\\n22: /// ```rust,ignore (pseudo-code)\\n23: /// my_macro! {\\n24: ///     // ...\\n25: ///     Literal {\\n26: ///         // ...\\n27: ///         fn character(ch: char) -> MySelf::Literal;\\n28: ///         // ...\\n29: ///         fn span(my_self: &MySelf::Literal) -> MySelf::Span;\\n30: ///         fn set_span(my_self: &mut MySelf::Literal, span: MySelf::Span);\\n31: ///     },\\n32: ///     // ...\\n33: /// }\\n34: /// ```\\n35: ///\\n36: /// The first two arguments serve to customize the arguments names\\n37: /// and argument/return types, to enable several different usecases:\\n38: ///\\n39: /// If `my_self` is just `self`, then each `fn` signature can be used\\n40: /// as-is for a method. If it's anything else (`self_` in practice),\\n41: /// then the signatures don't have a special `self` argument, and\\n42: /// can, therefore, have a different one introduced.\\n43: ///\\n44: /// If `MySelf` is just `Self`, then the types are only valid inside\\n45: /// a trait or a trait impl, where the trait has associated types\\n46: /// for each of the API types. If non-associated types are desired,\\n47: /// a module name (`self` in practice) can be used instead of `Self`.\\n48: macro_rules! with_api {\\n49:     ($S:ident, $self:ident, $m:ident) => {\\n50: //! Internal interface for communicating between a `proc_macro` client\n2: //! (a proc macro crate) and a `proc_macro` server (a compiler front-end).\n3: //!\n4: //! Serialization (with C ABI buffers) and unique integer handles are employed\n5: //! to allow safely interfacing between two copies of `proc_macro` built\n6: //! (from the same source) by different compilers with potentially mismatching\n7: //! Rust ABIs (e.g., stage0/bin/rustc vs stage1/bin/rustc during bootstrap).\n8: \n9: #![deny(unsafe_code)]\n10: \n11: use std::hash::Hash;\n12: use std::ops::{Bound, Range};\n13: use std::sync::Once;\n14: use std::{fmt, marker, mem, panic, thread};\n15: \n16: use crate::{Delimiter, Level, Spacing};\n17: \n18: /// Higher-order macro describing the server RPC API, allowing automatic\n19: /// generation of type-safe Rust APIs, both client-side and server-side.\n20: ///\n21: /// `with_api!(MySelf, my_self, my_macro)` expands to:\n22: /// ```rust,ignore (pseudo-code)\n23: /// my_macro! {\n24: ///     // ...\n25: ///     Literal {\n26: ///         // ...\n27: ///         fn character(ch: char) -> MySelf::Literal;\n28: ///         // ...\n29: ///         fn span(my_self: &MySelf::Literal) -> MySelf::Span;\n30: ///         fn set_span(my_self: &mut MySelf::Literal, span: MySelf::Span);\n31: ///     },\n32: ///     // ...\n33: /// }\n34: /// ```\n35: ///\n36: /// The first two arguments serve to customize the arguments names\n37: /// and argument/return types, to enable several different usecases:\n38: ///\n39: /// If `my_self` is just `self`, then each `fn` signature can be used\n40: /// as-is for a method. If it's anything else (`self_` in practice),\n41: /// then the signatures don't have a special `self` argument, and\n42: /// can, therefore, have a different one introduced.\n43: ///\n44: /// If `MySelf` is just `Self`, then the types are only valid inside\n45: /// a trait or a trait impl, where the trait has associated types\n46: /// for each of the API types. If non-associated types are desired,\n47: /// a module name (`self` in practice) can be used instead of `Self`.\n48: macro_rules! with_api {\n49:     ($S:ident, $self:ident, $m:ident) => {\n50: \"1.29.0\")]\n926: pub enum Spacing {\n927:     /// A `Punct` token can join with the following token to form a multi-character operator.\n928:     ///\n929:     /// In token streams constructed using proc macro interfaces, `Joint` punctuation tokens can be\n930:     /// followed by any other tokens. However, in token streams parsed from source code, the\n931:     /// compiler will only set spacing to `Joint` in the following cases.\n932:     /// - When a `Punct` is immediately followed by another `Punct` without a whitespace. E.g. `+`\n933:     ///   is `Joint` in `+=` and `++`.\n934:     /// - When a single quote `'` is immediately followed by an identifier without a whitespace.\n935:     ///   E.g. `'` is `Joint` in `'lifetime`.\n936:     ///\n937:     /// This list may be extended in the future to enable more token combinations.\n938:     #[stable(feature = \"proc_macro_lib2\", since = \"1.29.0\")]\n939:     Joint,\n940:     /// A `Punct` token cannot join with the following token to form a multi-character operator.\n941:     ///\n942:     /// `Alone` punctuation tokens can be followed by any other tokens. In token streams parsed\n943:     /// from source code, the compiler will set spacing to `Alone` in all cases not covered by the\n944:     /// conditions for `Joint` above. E.g. `+` is `Alone` in `+ =`, `+ident` and `+()`. In\n945:     /// particular, tokens not followed by anything will be marked as `Alone`.\n946:     #[stable(feature = \"proc_macro_lib2\", since = \"1.29.0\")]\n947:     Alone,\n948: }\n949: \n950:
